  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f6d9168d-67e3-48b0-ae50-de956e3d2e0e'
      });

  <span id="freeText16143200606420259644" style="display:none">Darkness falls on the Great Green and the Ancient World is fiercely divided.<br /><br />On the killing fields outside the golden city of Troy, forces loyal to the Mykene King<b> Agamemnon</b> mass.<br /><br />Among them is <b>Odysseus</b>, fabled storyteller and reluctant ally to the Mykene. He knows that Agamemnon will stop at nothing to secure the treasure that lies within the city walls, and he must soon face his former friends in deadly combat.<br /><br />Ailing and bitter, the Trojan king waits. His hope is pinned on two heroes: his favourite son, <b>Hektor</b>, the mightiest warrior of his age, and the dread <b>Helikaon,</b> who will wreak terrible vengeance for the death of his wife at Mykene hands.<br /><br /><br />War has been declared.<br /><br /><br />As enemies, who are also kinsmen, are filled with bloodlust, they know that some of them - men and women - will become heroes: heroes who will live for ever in a story that will echo down the centuries.</span>

<a href="/questions/523818-so-is-it-implied-that-odysseus"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So... is it implied that Odysseus, Kalliades, and Skorpios all died due to the volcanic eruption at Thera? I didn't really understand the epilogue's description of what happened with Odysseus and Penelope. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/82746550-mohammed-jafri"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1561788913i/82746550._UX100_CR0,24,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/82746550-mohammed-jafri">Mohammed Jafri</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Like Shima said, the answer depends on the reader. <br />However, if you prefer to follow the work of Homer succeeding "Iliad" (on which the novel is based)<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Like Shima said, the answer depends on the reader. <br />However, if you prefer to follow the work of Homer succeeding "Iliad" (on which the novel is based) - "Odyssey"; Odysseus does not die. Rather, once the war was over he sailed back for Ithaca but got lost along the way. It took him ten whole years to finally return to Ithaca because Poseidon (who was angry at him) tried to kill him at sea. <br /><br />All the adventures that Odysseus speaks of in his stories, are indications to the ones he bared in this epic journey. <br /><br />Sadly, his crew never makes it home in the epic. They all die and Odysseus is the only one to return. So, Skorpios and Kalliades might actually have died.<br /><a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128225726" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128225726?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128225726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4674497104098518599"><b>IT IS OFFICIAL…</b>David Gemmell has written the <b>BESTEST</b> and most <b>HEROIEST</b> fantasy trilogy...ever....EVER. <br/><br/>I just finished this third installment of the epic Troy trilogy by the late (and sorely missed) David Gemmell and all I can say is that if you loved the first two, you will love this one. If you haven’t read the first two books, then you might want to take a long serious look in the mirror and reconsider some of your recent life choices as you may have taken a wrong turn somewhere. However, nev</span>
  <span id="freeText4674497104098518599" style="display:none"><b>IT IS OFFICIAL…</b>David Gemmell has written the <b>BESTEST</b> and most <b>HEROIEST</b> fantasy trilogy...ever....EVER. <br /><br />I just finished this third installment of the epic Troy trilogy by the late (and sorely missed) David Gemmell and all I can say is that if you loved the first two, you will love this one. If you haven’t read the first two books, then you might want to take a long serious look in the mirror and reconsider some of your recent life choices as you may have taken a wrong turn somewhere. However, never fear, it is not too late. Just drop what you are doing and GO BUY THEM.....NOW!!!!<br /><br />In this final installment, the battle lines have been drawn, some major battles and minor skirmishes have occurred and the final Siege of the City of Troy is ready to begin. <br /><br /><b><u>IN THIS CORNER</u>:</b> <br /><br />Agamemnon: The power-hungry Mykene King; <br />Achilles: Warrior Supremo and badass numero uno; <br />Odysseus: the honorable and brilliant tactician who Fate has made Agamemnon’s reluctant ally; and <br />Ajax, the Bone-splitter....guess what he does. <br /><br /><b><u>AND IN THIS CORNER</u>:</b> <br /><br />Priam: The less than honorable ruler of Troy; <br />Helikaon (now called Aeneas): King of Dardania and dangerously Hulk-tempered when pushed too far; <br />Hektor: Prince of Troy and second greatest warrior in the world (save for Achilles); <br />Gershon (aka Ahmose): The exiled prince of Egypt whose destiny finally catches up with him in stunning fashion; Banokles and Kalliades: Two former officers and stone killers of the Mykene army who now serve Troy; and<br />Andromache: Wife of Hektor and lover of Aeneas (I know what you are thinking but its complicated). <br /><br />And many, many more supporting characters on both sides. Oh....oh.....The Epicness is Awesome!!!!!<br /><br />Okay, everything about this book was transcendant in its testosterone-fueled greatness but I do want to specifically mention one aspect that I thought was especially well done. This series deals with an historical event (the fall of Troy) that is fairly well known, at least in a popular sense (thank you Homer), despite the minimal amount of historical records on the subject. Gemmell manages to include all of the famous “elements” of the Troy saga, but he does so in such a fresh, original way that the story feels completely new while still making sense within the popularly understood historical frame of reference. <br /><br />I will give you one example <i>(don’t worry…no spoilers)</i>: I assume everyone knows the story of the Trojan Horse. Well Gemmell includes this element in the story, but his depiction is so unique and credible way that the reader (at least me) (a) doesn’t recognize it as such until it's actually happening and (b) once the scene occurs, the reader (again at least me) is left thinking, ‘Oh...shit...I can completely see how this event over time would become the “legend” of the Trojan Horse.’<br /><br />The execution was....BRILLIANT!!! <br /><br />In addition, the way that Gemmell expands the story to include characters and events that are remembered in world history outside the narrative arc of the fall of Troy was simply amazing and added real epic depth to the story. <br /><br />Of course, I do have one NEGATIVE thing to say about this book and the series which may seem pretty obvious. <br /><br /><b>Itmade me feel really, really sucky about myself!! </b> <br /><br />Not exactly the kind of book you want to pick up if you are struggling with your self-esteem. These guys (and girls) are at the pinnacle of bravery, loyalty, honor and overall <b>badassedness</b> and I kept feeling like the last one chosen at recess when the kids are picking kickball teams. Apart from that personal self-image speed bump, this is as fun and enjoyable as it gets and I give it my HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION!!!<br /><br />6.0 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4674497104098518599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2542716451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2542716451" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2542716451?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345477040" href="/book/show/3928308-troy">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Greek mythology &amp; historical fiction fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2542716451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11528209246181682390"><b>The end of the Trojan War is here, did Gemmell delivered a satisfying conclusion in his final work?</b><br/><br/>The answer to that will be mostly yes, and a few sections of no. I’m honestly quite conflicted about <i>Fall of Kings.</i> This is the last book in the <i>Troy</i> trilogy by David Gemmell, it’s also his final work before he passed away that ended up being finished by his wife, Stella Gemmell. Because this is his final work, there’s a part of me that really want to give this book a full 5 stars but I can’t due t</span>
  <span id="freeText11528209246181682390" style="display:none"><b>The end of the Trojan War is here, did Gemmell delivered a satisfying conclusion in his final work?</b><br /><br />The answer to that will be mostly yes, and a few sections of no. I’m honestly quite conflicted about <i>Fall of Kings.</i> This is the last book in the <i>Troy</i> trilogy by David Gemmell, it’s also his final work before he passed away that ended up being finished by his wife, Stella Gemmell. Because this is his final work, there’s a part of me that really want to give this book a full 5 stars but I can’t due to a few problems I had with it. I’ll divide this review into two simple parts: parts that worked first and then parts that didn’t.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Trust your instincts, and make judgements on what your heart tells you. The heart will not betray you.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Firstly, the prose. Same as the first two books, the writing was once again top-notch. If I didn’t know better, I wouldn’t have known that Stella Gemmell took part in the writing of this book; it totally felt like David Gemmell was still the one who wrote it completely. Second, the last 30% of the book which encompassed the final battle of the Trojan War was awesome. Hector vs Achilles was absolutely amazing. I’m serious. I’ve been waiting for the final duel between these two prominent figures since the first book and Gemmell wrote their duel with expertly that it ended up being one of the best duels I’ve ever read. It was superb, intense, compelling, and I completely lost track of time because of the breathtaking battle and drama that unfolds during this sequence. The characters of the trilogy felt real and the conclusion was also satisfying. Plus, Gemmell did a great reimagining on the “Trojan Horse” event that became the signal fire that took down the city of Troy. Finally, I must say that I’m pleasantly surprised by how much I ended up caring about Kalliades and Banokles. I was super bored with their one hundred pages introduction at the beginning of <i>Shield of Thunder</i>, I didn’t realize that they would end up being some of the best characters from this trilogy alongside Hector and Odysseus. Not Helikaon the main character? Exactly.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I was a man before I was a king, and no true man walks away when a friend needs him.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Helikaon was amazing in the first book. However, since the second book, I feel like he’s becoming much more of a side character compared to the other characters. One huge example for this is that in the last battle of the Trojan War, Kalliades and Banokles were there entirely and they did a lot of bloodbath battles while Helikaon appeared very briefly to literally climb. And then there was the matter of Gershom’s story ended up being super bizarre and out of place. After finishing this and letting it sit for a few hours, I honestly don’t know what the purpose of his storyline was. Finally, I don’t think it was really necessary to have this series being a trilogy; two books should’ve been enough. I found that there were quite plenty of sections within the last two books that didn’t really add any value to the storyline.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Hate is the father of all evil.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Overall though, I very much enjoyed reading through this trilogy despite a few issues I had along the way. Although the Trojan War came from Greek Mythology, Gemmell turned the narrative completely to a historical fiction style; close to zero magic, no gods or demigods appearances. I know that I started reading Gemmell’s work from his final trilogy, and after enjoying this one, I won’t dispute the possibility that I will backtrack through his work and start from the beginning, <i>Legend</i>. <i>Fall of Kings</i> was an incredible read, it's Gemmell's final work and it's a great one. I highly recommend this trilogy to any fans of historical fiction and Greek Mythology.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Series Review:</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>Lord of the Silver Bow</i>: <u>
  <b>
    <a href="http://novelnotions.net/2018/11/15/lord-of-the-silver-bow/" rel="nofollow noopener">4.5/5 stars</a>
  </b>
</u><br /><i>Shield of Thunder</i>: <u>
  <b>
    <a href="http://novelnotions.net/2018/11/17/shield-of-thunder-troy-2/" rel="nofollow noopener">4/5 stars</a>
  </b>
</u><br /><i>Fall of Kings</i>: <b>
  <u>4/5 stars</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>Troy</i>: <b>
  <u>12.5/15 stars</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>You can buy the book with free shipping by clicking this <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780345477040/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">link!</a></u></b><br /><br /><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2018/11/22/fall-of-kings-troy-3/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>

<div id="review_1919035028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1919035028" />
    <a title="Anish Kohli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli"><img alt="Anish Kohli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579696384p2/20963257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1919035028?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anish Kohli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anish Kohli" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli">Anish Kohli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1919035028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1004745113788412826">I can't....I won't....I don't.....Just....Just can't. Not right now.<br/><br/>After a long while, years actually, and almost a huge number of books later, I have finished a series that has me at a total loss for words. <br/>It has been such a ride. So many ups and downs. So many deaths. So much love. Such love. Such ferocious love, the one that threatens to destroy everything if shattered. Friendship. Respect. So many emotions I have no words to say it all. <br/>Just that I am low right now that this series has end</span>
  <span id="freeText1004745113788412826" style="display:none">I can't....I won't....I don't.....Just....Just can't. Not right now.<br /><br />After a long while, years actually, and almost a huge number of books later, I have finished a series that has me at a total loss for words. <br />It has been such a ride. So many ups and downs. So many deaths. So much love. Such love. Such ferocious love, the one that threatens to destroy everything if shattered. Friendship. Respect. So many emotions I have no words to say it all. <br />Just that I am low right now that this series has ended. I’ve only felt this a couple of times before. And this feeling, the end of a journey, THIS feeling, the despair and happiness mixed in right amounts is the reason I have been and will always be a SERIES reader. I need that connection with my characters and 1 book is not sufficient. <br /><br />It broke my heart to know that the author couldn’t complete this series. It will haunt me to know that he couldn’t see it through and passed away. His wife completed this book and concluded the series. I have a complaint. Just the one. But after such a great trilogy, I would be a petty man to voice it.<br /><br />I have love and respect for David Gemmell. I will die if I do not read more of his works sometime soon. <br /><br />I do not know how to review this book. I probably can’t. No, I definitely can’t. But it would be a damn shame if I never told the words that I fell in love with. <br /><br />I will leave you all with a few of the gems I found in this book. <br /><br /><b><br />“War makes brutes of us all and it is sometimes hard to tell the difference between insanity and cold-blooded brutality.”<br /><br />“By the gods, boy, no one wants to see the truth of war. They want to see heroes, tall and strong, striking and handsome.”<br /><br />“It is said that the gates of paradise can only be opened by the tears of those left behind. I do not know whether that be true. It should be, I think.”<br /><br />“At this moment war and perhaps death seemed wonderfully simple. It was life that was so hard.”<br /><br /><i>“What could he say? That all his life he had dreamed of finding love and that she was the embodiment of that dream? That every day since he had met her she had been in his heart? That upon falling asleep at night her face shimmered in his mind, and upon waking his first thoughts were of her?”</i><br /><br />“We’ve seen a lot of death, you and I — more than most. You know as well as I do death doesn’t always come to those who deserve it.”<br /><br />“Until then, though, he had had no idea what love was. And arrogantly, he had believed the choice of marriage always would be his. He never had dreamed he would fall helplessly in love with someone who was unavailable, already betrothed to his closest friend. The gods watch for such arrogance with glee, he thought.”<br /><br /><i>“She was his north star, the fixed point around which his world turned. For as long as his heart beat, or hers, he believed they would share a destiny.”</i><br /><br />“They never should have killed him, you see. Hektor and Achilles were the last great heroes. And after the Age of Heroes comes the Age of Darkness.”<br /></b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1004745113788412826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1263652824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1263652824" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23206148-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473945175p2/23206148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1263652824?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/23206148-terence">Terence</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1263652824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10824004386958292529"><u>How Fall of Kings <i><b>should have ended</b></i></u><br/><br/><blockquote>(<b>Note:</b> All endings are written by me in an homage to <br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/user/HISHEdotcom' rel='nofollow noopener'>How it Should Have Ended</a>. They aren't spoilers, none of this stuff happened although I would've enjoyed any of these endings more than the actual ending.)<br/><br/><b><u>Possible ending #1</u></b><br/><br/><i>"Lord Helikaon," said Khalkeus.<br/>"What is it Khalkeus? I'm busy with preparation for our next steps in the war with the Mykene," said Helikaon.<br/>"That's what this is about Lord. I've found a way to massively increase the range of your ships fir</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10824004386958292529" style="display:none"><u>How Fall of Kings <i><b>should have ended</b></i></u><br /><br /><blockquote>(<b>Note:</b> All endings are written by me in an homage to <br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/HISHEdotcom" rel="nofollow noopener">How it Should Have Ended</a>. They aren't spoilers, none of this stuff happened although I would've enjoyed any of these endings more than the actual ending.)<br /><br /><b><u>Possible ending #1</u></b><br /><br /><i>"Lord Helikaon," said Khalkeus.<br />"What is it Khalkeus? I'm busy with preparation for our next steps in the war with the Mykene," said Helikaon.<br />"That's what this is about Lord. I've found a way to massively increase the range of your ships fire hurlers. The increase will enable the ship to throw fire for miles rather than a few hundred feet," replied Khalkeus.<br />"Do it then Khalkeus," Helikaon said while his icy blue eyes saw right through Khalkeus.<br /><br /><b>Fast forward to the siege of Troy</b><br /><br />"We are close enough now to burn the sieging Mykene army to the ground," said Oniacus.<br />"Let's rain fire on Agammenon's ambition and end his reign of evil," said Helikaon.<br />The jars of nephthar were hurled for miles shattering into the armies of the west as men were soaked. Then the fire flew through the air for what seemed like days before it finally ignited and burned Agamemnon's ambition and men to ashes.<br /><br /><b><u>Possible ending #2</u></b><br /><br />"Come do your daughterly duty Andromache," Priam said while groping all over her body.<br />Suddenly Hektor stepped around the corner.<br />"Father I was speaking with my brothers and we are tired of you raping our wives. So we decided to give Agammenon exactly what he wants you, your gold, and your city," Hektor said with a tone as cold as winter.<br />"My son you can't mean...." Priam mumbled as the Eagles and Antiphones bound and gagged him.<br /><br /><b>Fast forward to the armies of the west arriving at Troy</b><br /><br />"There are no men, women, children, or animals to be seen," Achilles said.<br />"Battle King, Battle King," a soldier screamed as he ran to Agammenon. "You must see this my King."<br />They all headed into the unlocked doors of Troy to find Priam bound and gagged sitting in his treasury with a parchment on his chest that read, "We surrender the city and the gold as you demanded and included the King Priam as a bonus." It was signed by all Priam's sons, daughters, grandson/sons, and granddaughter/daughters.<br /><br /><b><u>Possible ending #3</u></b><br /><br />"You are a coward Achilles," Agammenon sprayed spit as he snarled the words.<br />Achilles said nothing, but in the time it takes a man to sneeze he drew his sword and decapitated Agammenon with his head making a heavy thud sound as it hit the wall. Achilles scanned the speechless crowd, shrugged his massive shoulders, and said "Come now, I can't be the only one who was thinking about doing that." <br />All the men in the meeting except Menelaus laughed. Odysseus laughed so hard wine came out his nose and he couldn't regain his composure. </i></blockquote><br /><br />In Fall of Kings and the entire trilogy David Gemmell really captured Odysseus well and that was the strongest part of the series. The rest of the series was fairly plain and average.<br /><br />My biggest gripes have to be Gershom's storyline and the epilogue. I really don't see the point of the detour Gershom's story became. It doesn't fit the book or the story at all. It's inclusion just seemed pointless. The epilogue was a rushed attempt to show the future yet it didn't really add anything of value to the story.<br /> <br />The Fall of Kings was an adequate conclusion to the retelling of the Trojan War.</span>

<div id="review_584133063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/584133063" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/584133063?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer584133063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15321925169870083281">Originally reviewed at <a href='http://bookwraiths.com/2013/07/31/very-good-ending/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths Reviews</a> <br/><br/><i>Troy: Fall of Kings</i> is the end of David Gemmell's epic historical series, and here a reader will find portrayed the final days of the Trojan War, the duel between Hektor and Achilles, the Trojan Horse, and the fall of mighty Troy. Without a doubt, the novel dazzles in its realistic portrayal of these historical events, leaving one both in awe of its brilliance and perplexed by its obvious flaws. <br/><br/>The good parts of the novel are easy to point out. David G</span>
  <span id="freeText15321925169870083281" style="display:none">Originally reviewed at <a href="http://bookwraiths.com/2013/07/31/very-good-ending/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths Reviews</a> <br /><br /><i>Troy: Fall of Kings</i> is the end of David Gemmell's epic historical series, and here a reader will find portrayed the final days of the Trojan War, the duel between Hektor and Achilles, the Trojan Horse, and the fall of mighty Troy. Without a doubt, the novel dazzles in its realistic portrayal of these historical events, leaving one both in awe of its brilliance and perplexed by its obvious flaws. <br /><br />The good parts of the novel are easy to point out. David Gemmell and his wife (Who I understand finished said book after her husband’s death.) did an outstanding job of portraying realistic characters, who fit perfectly into the historical narrative of this period. These characters behave realistic based upon their established personality, and some of them almost burst off the page in their brilliance. The same can be said about the combat scenes in <i>Fall of Kings</i>, because they radiate ultra realism as the Greek and Trojan warriors exude fear and adrenaline while clashing in ancient combat. Even the final duel between Hector and Achilles is superbly done, penned in such detailed and dramatic fashion that it must stand as one of the best portrayed combats between heroic warriors in all of literature. And we must not forget the final “Trojan Horse” resolution, which might be the most well thought out and simplest solutions I've ever encountered.<br /><br />No matter how well the Gemmell's did some things, however, there are still obvious flaws with the story. Helikaon and Andromache, in particular, make certain decision that do not ring true to their characterization throughout the series and seem forced so that other important moments in history can be written about. Another is the resolution - if you can even call it that - of Gershom’s strange plot line that was somewhat mystifying throughout the series. There are other examples of characters just disappearing or behaving strangely throughout the later part of the book, especially the last few chapters where Troy’s survivors are shown fleeing for their lives, but I do not want to belabor the point, only point out that these moments detract from the effect of the narrative as a whole.<br /><br />With all that being said, I enjoyed the novel. It was a fitting ending to a good series. A trilogy where the Gemmells did an excellent job of taking the myths about Troy and turning them into compelling historical fiction. Not to say they did not take artistic liberties with historical fact, but that, even though they did, it rang more or less true. For attempting to shed a light of reason on the Trojan War, this novel and series is a must read for lovers of historical fiction. <br /><br />Finally, I would be remise if I did not salute the legendary David Gemmell. There will never be another writer who can do justice to a warrior’s true spirit as he did in this series and all his novels. A final triumph for a true master of his craft! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15321925169870083281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_292273612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292273612" />
    <a title="Erika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5666413-erika"><img alt="Erika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361128945p2/5666413.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292273612?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erika" href="/user/show/5666413-erika">Erika</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=done-series">done-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=favorite-female-character">favorite-female-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=favorite-male-character">favorite-male-character</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292273612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15420676886651505564">And this is it... <b>The end of this EPIC Troy trilogy.</b><br/><br/>Oh God, I'm sad. I didn't want this to end. When i finished it, i just closed the book and stared at the ceiling for several hours,... ok no, I'm kidding,... for several minutes and couldn't help but start thinking about life and death and war and human kind, and i just felt so sad. Sometimes people are so greedy and ambitious, and want to get everything and don't care how. It doesn't matter if, to get whatever they want, they'll end up leaving</span>
  <span id="freeText15420676886651505564" style="display:none">And this is it... <b>The end of this EPIC Troy trilogy.</b><br /><br />Oh God, I'm sad. I didn't want this to end. When i finished it, i just closed the book and stared at the ceiling for several hours,... ok no, I'm kidding,... for several minutes and couldn't help but start thinking about life and death and war and human kind, and i just felt so sad. Sometimes people are so greedy and ambitious, and want to get everything and don't care how. It doesn't matter if, to get whatever they want, they'll end up leaving a path of destruction, misery, ruins, loss, pain, death behind.<br /><br />I like the way it was described in one paragraph in the book:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"... After the Age of Heroes comes the Age of Darkness... Within a generation they will tear down the stone palaces of the mighty. In the Lion's Hall where the heroes walked there will be only rats and beetles feeding; then green grass will cover the ruins, and sheep will graze there."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Are all wars really necessary?, Do they do any good at all after all the destruction they cause?, In this example Troy was a mighty empire, there were some kings trying to bring it down to try to steal its treasury and in the process they were taking many lives to doom. And it all for what? <br /><br />Sad, as it is, the execution of this popular story was outstanding. All the events were believable, they looked like something that would happen in a real life situation, not with imaginary elements or unrealistic. I JUST LOVE IT.<br /><br />Really, these books are a must read, i can't believe the few ratings it's got here on goodreads. <b>This gem should be known</b>, Gemmell has given us a superb heroic fantasy tale, that even though I'm sorry to realize the author died a while ago, he'll still live through his characters, which are absolutely of <b>the best characters I've ever come across</b>. It's impossible not to relate with them, not to feel their sufferings, it might a couple of times bring tears to your eyes.<br /><br /><b>This is good writing, I'll for sure be reading more of his work. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15420676886651505564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_753377153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/753377153" />
    <a title="Kerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2570383-kerry"><img alt="Kerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573926586p2/2570383.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/753377153?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry" href="/user/show/2570383-kerry">Kerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2570383-kerry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2570383-kerry?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer753377153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3014226956699804372">An epic heroes farewell, or an epic farewell. This very readable and entertaining story has even more meaning for me when I learned Stella Gemmell completed this last book soon after her husband David's death. <br/><br/><i>Cathartic. Providing psychological relief through the open expression of strong emotions.</i><br/><br/>This is a long farewell. I could easily imagine that Stella was able to say goodbye to her hero David with every passage of this book. A silly romantic notion? Too idealistic or simplistic for me to th</span>
  <span id="freeText3014226956699804372" style="display:none">An epic heroes farewell, or an epic farewell. This very readable and entertaining story has even more meaning for me when I learned Stella Gemmell completed this last book soon after her husband David's death. <br /><br /><i>Cathartic. Providing psychological relief through the open expression of strong emotions.</i><br /><br />This is a long farewell. I could easily imagine that Stella was able to say goodbye to her hero David with every passage of this book. A silly romantic notion? Too idealistic or simplistic for me to think that? Perhaps, but 'Fall of Kings' is entirely about passing on and change.<br /><br />Kings die, heroes bid farewell to their comrades through life ending acts of self-sacrifice then succumb to their wounds, great cities fall and their people are slain or are scattered to the four winds, and while redemption is at hand, so is death.<br /><br />Odysseus's love for Penelope is so simple and total that he would walk recklessly into a room filled with would be killers because, for Odysseus, being rational is not rational when Penelope's life is at stake. Helikaon does not even consider danger when Andromache's life is at risk. <br /><br />A hero does not forcefully drag his followers into a lost cause but most still follow the hero because his actions are noble and pure. The hero allows others their own journey and wishes them farewell when they part ways, even it is against everyone's best judgment.<br /><br />Jedediah Purdy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/160767.For_Common_Things_Irony__Trust__and_Commitment_in_America_Today" title="For Common Things Irony, Trust, and Commitment in America Today by Jedediah Purdy" rel="nofollow noopener">For Common Things: Irony, Trust, and Commitment in America Today</a> calls Jerry Seinfeld, 'irony incarnate.' He has a 'style of speech and behavior that avoids all appearance of naivete -- of naive devotion, belief, or hope...' <br /><br />If true, 'Troy: Fall of Kings' is anti-Seinfeld. For Gemmell's heroes devotion, belief and hope are the only things worth their salt, naïve or not. All things considered, I gave Troy the fifth star because such a notion appeals me, naïve or not.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="3014226956699804372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2252047383717549319" style="display:none">An immensely readable trilogy, which kept me engaged from beginning to end, except perhaps for a couple of hundred pages in this book which described war, war and more war. <div id="review_78262061" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78262061" />
    <a title="Mihir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1229652-mihir"><img alt="Mihir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366908667p2/1229652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78262061?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mihir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mihir" href="/user/show/1229652-mihir">Mihir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1229652-mihir?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78262061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13191746609265779735"><br/> Read Fantasy Book Critic's article <a href='http://fantasybookcritic.blogspot.com/2009/08/trojan-war-reinterpretation-troy.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Trojan War - A Reinterpretation: "The Troy Trilogy" by David and Stella Gemmell </a><br/><br/> Mini-review of FALL OF KINGS: Sadly the world was poorer when David Gemmell passed away on 26th July 2006, condolence messages started pouring in & before anyone could speculate about what would happen to the third book, Stella Gemmell took it upon herself to complete her husband’s vision of Troy. She has assisted him in his previous books by doing research work & in the Troy </span>
  <span id="freeText13191746609265779735" style="display:none"><br /> Read Fantasy Book Critic's article <a href="http://fantasybookcritic.blogspot.com/2009/08/trojan-war-reinterpretation-troy.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Trojan War - A Reinterpretation: "The Troy Trilogy" by David and Stella Gemmell </a><br /><br /> Mini-review of FALL OF KINGS: Sadly the world was poorer when David Gemmell passed away on 26th July 2006, condolence messages started pouring in &amp; before anyone could speculate about what would happen to the third book, Stella Gemmell took it upon herself to complete her husband’s vision of Troy. She has assisted him in his previous books by doing research work &amp; in the Troy trilogy specifically focused her abilities on all the background material required for the preparation in making of the books. Also David had managed to write 60,000-70,000 words before Stella thought of debuting. Though she had no previous writing experience she did soldier on &amp; based on David’s notes for the entire series &amp; the last book. She finished the book on time &amp; it was set for publication.<br /><br />The 3rd book Fall of Kings was coauthored by both the Gemmells’ &amp; the beauty of it was that you could not differentiate between their voices. The story flowed smoothly beginning with the events set after fall of Thraki &amp; the beginning of the invasion of Troy by Agamemnon as he has coerced &amp; coaxed all of his allies into joining the attack on Troy.<br /><br />All the previous POV characters are back in this one and with the addition of a few new POVs such as Achilles, Xander, Skorpius, etc. I won’t like to specify what exactly happens as almost all of us have a general idea how this is going to end. The beauty of the Gemmellian plotting makes the read worthwhile &amp; manages to surprise the readers along the way with their twist on the myths of Troy.<br /><br />The ending while heartbreaking is a testimonial to Homer’s Troy with some cool alterations and the addition of Gershorm’s sub-plot makes it pretty intriguing as well. The epilogue is one of the best I have ever read &amp; can stand as a epithet to David, his talents &amp; his way of thinking &amp; is written emphatically by Stella Gemmell.<br /><br />Even though the trilogy ends with this book, the story &amp; characters will stay with you for a long time as its said “Storytellers never die, they live on in their stories”. We have been indeed fortunate to read David’s stories for nearly a quarter of a century. I can only imagine what could have been, if not for the tragic early demise. David Gemmell was one of the most inspirational writers ever to grace the world &amp; will always continue to enthrall readers eternally with his ideals, thoughts &amp; books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13191746609265779735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_512674586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/512674586" />
    <a title="L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6463881-l"><img alt="L" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/512674586?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L" href="/user/show/6463881-l">L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer512674586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5516008995864262269">A markedly noteworthy ending to an outstanding epic fantasy trilogy, that professes such remarkable depth! <br/><br/>David Gemmell has to be one of the greatest writers of all-time whose work is just so astonishing, that it outshines many within the increasingly diverse fantasy genre. His work is truly original and of such quality and profound substance, that his stories remain with you long after you have read them. Fall of Kings (Troy 3#) is the magnificent conclusion to a sweeping historical masterpiec</span>
  <span id="freeText5516008995864262269" style="display:none">A markedly noteworthy ending to an outstanding epic fantasy trilogy, that professes such remarkable depth! <br /><br />David Gemmell has to be one of the greatest writers of all-time whose work is just so astonishing, that it outshines many within the increasingly diverse fantasy genre. His work is truly original and of such quality and profound substance, that his stories remain with you long after you have read them. Fall of Kings (Troy 3#) is the magnificent conclusion to a sweeping historical masterpiece, which can only be described as pure perfection and sublime storytelling. As a fan of authors such as Conn Iggulden (Genghis Khan &amp; Caesar) and Bernard Cornwell, I thoroughly enjoyed this absorbing tale that was full of action and intense drama. I would certainly recommend this trilogy to those who enjoy historical works by authors mentioned above or Christian Cameron, Michael Jecks ect. as it incorporates stirring action, bloodthirsty battles and brave warriors amidst a compelling narrative of such great scope. <br /><br />The Ancient World is divided. On the killing fields outside of Troy, forces loyal to the Mykene King mass. Among them is Odysseus; a fabled storyteller and reluctant ally to the Mykene. The King’s task is to secure the treasure that lies within the city’s walls, and he will stop at nothing to carry out this task, including facing his former friends in deadly combat. <br />The Trojan King waits. His hopes are pinned on two individuals; his son Hektor (who is the mightiest warrior of his age) and the dread Helikaon (who is determined to gain vengeance on the death of his wife at Mykene’s hand). War has been declared…As enemies, who are also kinsmen, are filled with bloodlust; they know that some of them - men and women - will become heroes: heroes who will live for ever in a story that will echo down the centuries. <br /><br />This fantastic conclusion to an epic saga is just brilliant, and is as impacting as you would expect it to be – with twists and turns until the dramatic ending. Sat on the edge of my seat throughout I was lost within a world of heated conflict, bitter revenge and self-centered ambition that seeped into others like a poison and so corrupts those pure of heart whilst others fight for justice. The striking golden cover of this book ties-in with the tale that exudes magnificence, with the writing as ever being highly readable and exceptional. This wonderful tale by a most accomplished author is nail-bitingly gripping, full of shocking events and fueled by heated passion that is so strong it radiates off the page. <br /><br />A spectacular triumph and a trilogy that I shall be re-reading very soon!! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5516008995864262269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Rick Slane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17459218-rick-slane"><img alt="Rick Slane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552977455p2/17459218.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_75986749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75986749" />
    <a title="Karla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2846441-karla"><img alt="Karla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537371209p2/2846441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75986749?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla" href="/user/show/2846441-karla">Karla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345477040" href="/book/show/3928308-troy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2846441-karla?shelf=dead-tree">dead-tree</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75986749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2965496437346976478">Even though this trilogy failed to interest from the first book, I kept reading in hopes that it would improve. Sadly, it didn't, and I detected no decline or difference in quality when Gemmell's writing ended and his wife's began. The characterization continued to be shallow, the plot points far-fetched and for their own sake. I'm specifically thinking of the entire subplot of Gershom, which had nothing to do with the main story and had the feel of being a kitchen sink approach to bring in all </span>
  <span id="freeText2965496437346976478" style="display:none">Even though this trilogy failed to interest from the first book, I kept reading in hopes that it would improve. Sadly, it didn't, and I detected no decline or difference in quality when Gemmell's writing ended and his wife's began. The characterization continued to be shallow, the plot points far-fetched and for their own sake. I'm specifically thinking of the entire subplot of Gershom, which had nothing to do with the main story and had the feel of being a kitchen sink approach to bring in all the legends of the era. It felt tacked on, if not tacky. What was the point of it? Darned if I know. I finally settled on "pointless and pretentious." Likewise was the final scene of Andromache in the outpost of Ancient Rome. After nearly 3 books of such cheap tricks, it was an expected reveal that held no surprise. The device had, by that point, achieved glib triteness and the well had long since gone dry.<br /><br />Most every character remained one-dimensional (in rare flashes two), and they were kept to the page. They didn't come into my head to play and act out the story, a situation probably due to the fact that apart from occasional mentions of hair color, build shape, and whether eyes flashed cold or angry, there wasn't much physical description. When there was, it was generic and not very evocative. Psychologically, the majority of the cast were ciphers.<br /><br />Again, constant deviations into past perfect flashbacks during scenes to reveal pertinent details to make a scene work were irritating and had a slapdash tone that pervaded the book. The entire invasion of Ithaka by pirates and the captivity of Penelope would have been a great sequence both in action and drama, yet it was merely summarized by Penelope's inner voice as she sits tied to her throne. If this had been the only instance, fine, but it wasn't. Too much was revealed as memories, not as present action. There were too few scenes that dragged me right into the action, the only exception I can name being the breaching of King's Joy fortress. However, that scene was destroyed soon after by the risible dispatching of Paris &amp; Helen. (I am not a fan of Paris &amp; Helen in mythology, but their inept and gross handling by Gemmell had me clamoring to be their advocate.)<br /><br />Odysseus remained a full-bodied and engaging character, the only one to do so throughout all three books. The love between he and Penelope was touched upon in some tender asides, but it was much too little. They were the only couple I became attached to throughout the trilogy, and good as their scenes were, it can't even begin to elevate my opinion of the series as a whole.<br /><br />Final summary: Generic fantasy elements with the banal standards of the genre. The names are familiar, but they've been manipulated and twisted to suit the imported fantasy tropes to such a degree that they might as well have been named something else and correctly marketed as "Fantasy."</span>
  <a data-text-id="2965496437346976478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_151859517" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151859517" />
    <a title="Iset" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4973578-iset"><img alt="Iset" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563895104p2/4973578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151859517?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iset" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iset" href="/user/show/4973578-iset">Iset</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4973578-iset?shelf=bronze-age-5000-to-1100bce-fiction">bronze-age-5000-to-1100bce-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151859517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5481423621696500849">Once again, forgive the brevity of this review, but much of what I had to say about this last novel in the trilogy I have already presented in my review of the first book. I must admit, there was a note of concern going into this final instalment – <i>Fall of Kings</i> was sadly left as an unfinished work by David Gemmell’s passing, and his widow Stella used his notes to complete the novel and see it to publication. Obviously, I was somewhat concerned that there might be a visible join in the novel whe</span>
  <span id="freeText5481423621696500849" style="display:none">Once again, forgive the brevity of this review, but much of what I had to say about this last novel in the trilogy I have already presented in my review of the first book. I must admit, there was a note of concern going into this final instalment – <i>Fall of Kings</i> was sadly left as an unfinished work by David Gemmell’s passing, and his widow Stella used his notes to complete the novel and see it to publication. Obviously, I was somewhat concerned that there might be a visible join in the novel where David’s writing ended and Stella’s began, in two completely disparate styles, but there simply wasn’t. I couldn’t distinguish between the two styles of writing or discern where one ended and the other began, and this was excellent news as it really keeps the flow of the novel going and helped it to retain its cohesion and purpose. If anything, we encounter even more action and adventure than in the previous novels, as the overarching plotline reaches its climax with the unfolding of the Trojan War and the thematic tearing down of the establishment of previous instalments. The eventual fate of Helikaon and Andromache was not a surprise to me, but only because I’d been keeping the established mythos in mind, not because I expected it – Gemmell altered a fair bit of the Aeneas story throughout this trilogy, so much so that I wasn’t certain Aeneas’ tale would be wrapped up in concordance with "canon". However the eventual fate of characters such as Kalliades and Odysseus is left a mystery, and certainly wasn’t predictable – to the point where I almost wished, just because I connected with those characters so much, that there could have been a little bit more resolution. The fate of certain other characters was definitely surprising, and deviated a great deal from the "canon" of Homer and other ancient story-tellers, but it came across as surprising and interesting rather than an unacceptable alteration. The sheer pace and action of <i>Fall of Kings</i> really made it a rip-roaring read too – I was torn between wanting to find out what happened next and drawing out the moment when I’d have finished reading the trilogy! It actually inspired me to get a hold of Gemmell’s duology about Parmenion, just so that I could once again enjoy Gemmell’s absorbing story-telling style in an historical setting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5481423621696500849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1609288973" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609288973" />
    <a title="Shima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20404643-shima"><img alt="Shima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468228684p2/20404643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1609288973?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shima" href="/user/show/20404643-shima">Shima</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780552151139" href="/book/show/1850100.Fall_of_Kings">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1609288973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1504011950355705044">First of all I'm extremely embarrassed about how long it took me to finish this. I can't remember the last time it took me more than three days to read a book. However as I did move to another continent and start university, I think I can be forgiven this time. <br/><br/>I'm really unsure about what to say about this book. Stella Gemmell does a great job of finishing this book. Yet, I couldn't help but feel it somehow wasn't quite as connected and spectacular as Gemmell's other works. I wasn't happy with </span>
  <span id="freeText1504011950355705044" style="display:none">First of all I'm extremely embarrassed about how long it took me to finish this. I can't remember the last time it took me more than three days to read a book. However as I did move to another continent and start university, I think I can be forgiven this time. <br /><br />I'm really unsure about what to say about this book. Stella Gemmell does a great job of finishing this book. Yet, I couldn't help but feel it somehow wasn't quite as connected and spectacular as Gemmell's other works. I wasn't happy with Gresham and Khalkeus's story lines. Also maybe just the fact that I knew it wasn't written by him made me feel this way and it's mostly in my head, I don't know. <br /><br />If you look at it rationally there is nothing lacking in this book, yet emotionally somehow it didn't have the same impact on me as Gemmell always does. That meaning it was still better than most other books, but it only left me teary eyed and not outright crying, which is a first for a Gemmel book.<br /><br />What really did make a impact on me was the last bit written by Conn Iggulden for David Gemmell. It's hard to know this was the last book he will ever write. I can't help but think how many more he had written by now had he been alive. Writer's like Gemmell can't be compared with others or be criticized like them, Gemmell can write the same exact plot as another author and something that is considered a flaw there will turn into something beautiful under his pen. A flat one dimensional characters turns into someone you care about, he can even make you adore an instant love. <br /><br />Gemmell truly was a master, the world of literature is a sadder and emptier place without him and no one else can do what he could. Gemmell touched something deep inside of you. Gemmell made an impact. Gemmell made you laugh and cry and fall in love. I'm in his debt, I wouldn't be the person I am if I hadn't started reading his books as a child. <br /><br /><b>"Story tellers never die as long as their stories live on" </b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1504011950355705044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_274943287" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274943287" />
    <a title="Sue Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3583076-sue-smith"><img alt="Sue Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272665985p2/3583076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274943287?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue Smith" href="/user/show/3583076-sue-smith">Sue Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3583076-sue-smith?shelf=books-read-in-2012">books-read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274943287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5692722957121272166">Such a great book. Such a great series. I can't remember when I've enjoyed a series as much as this one. Of course, being based on one of the world's best known historical story, it's not hard to see why it's so intriguing. But it's a book that's written beyond that, and for that reason alone - it's well worth the effort to read it all.<br/><br/>What I mean by that comment - that it's written beyond the historical story - is that he's taken the slant of the story that we all recall of Troy and made it som</span>
  <span id="freeText5692722957121272166" style="display:none">Such a great book. Such a great series. I can't remember when I've enjoyed a series as much as this one. Of course, being based on one of the world's best known historical story, it's not hard to see why it's so intriguing. But it's a book that's written beyond that, and for that reason alone - it's well worth the effort to read it all.<br /><br />What I mean by that comment - that it's written beyond the historical story - is that he's taken the slant of the story that we all recall of Troy and made it somewhat easier to swallow - so we can see looking back through our modern eyes and see a reality of what it probably was like to actually 'be' in the middle of a time of heros and gods. And it really made it easy to see how a story can become something completely else as it gets retold over time through countless people and ages. I loved it.<br /><br />Fantastic characters and a really interesting commentary on how war can be such a wasteful thing (even though that's really not part of the book). You really get wrapped up on each ones' fates as the story unfolds and you always hope for the best - even though you know the outcome. <br /><br />Highest recommendations on this series. I'll be sure to pick up more of David Gemmell's work!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5692722957121272166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1273447944" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1273447944" />
    <a title="Elizabeth A" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3123067-elizabeth-a"><img alt="Elizabeth A" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420475630p2/3123067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1273447944?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth A" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth A" href="/user/show/3123067-elizabeth-a">Elizabeth A</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3123067-elizabeth-a?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1273447944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16270076366071587587">This, the final book in the Troy Trilogy is a rollicking good ride. The author died before completing this one, so his wife took over, and while I can tell where the transition happened, I enjoyed every moment of this story.<br/><br/>The authors change some of the "facts" of the story, but I was OK with it. I particularly liked how the death of Hektor was done in this version (that should not be a spoiler people). Since that was one of the tough parts of the story for me (never mind the hundreds of thousa</span>
  <span id="freeText16270076366071587587" style="display:none">This, the final book in the Troy Trilogy is a rollicking good ride. The author died before completing this one, so his wife took over, and while I can tell where the transition happened, I enjoyed every moment of this story.<br /><br />The authors change some of the "facts" of the story, but I was OK with it. I particularly liked how the death of Hektor was done in this version (that should not be a spoiler people). Since that was one of the tough parts of the story for me (never mind the hundreds of thousands of deaths!), I appreciated this touch. Pages before the battle between Hektor and Achilles, I found myself slowing way down, as I did not want to get to that scene. There are tie-ins with some other myths that I also found interesting - the plagues of Egypt in particular. The ending was a little too happily-ever-after for my tastes - but after all those battles and death, I guess a little happy isn't too much to ask for.<br /><br />The epic saga and the age of heroes draws to a close in this book. There are acts of bravery and courage, betrayal and cowardice, insanity and beauty, love and loss. Those Greeks sure knew how to capture the essence of the human condition. So good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16270076366071587587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167684259" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167684259" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5341034-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422650667p2/5341034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167684259?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/5341034-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5341034-dawn?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5341034-dawn?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5341034-dawn?shelf=fantasy-alternate">fantasy-alternate</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167684259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17469724942856436210">This is the last book in a trilogy about the Trojan War.<br/>The entire synopsis of this book can be summed up by saying it's a book of war. It is, in it's entirety, a book of battles, small and large. <br/>I have enjoyed the entire series. It is filled with epic battles and epic heroes, strong women and brave warriors, death and life. Where some of my favorite characters die and some live.<br/>And in the end, it was a fabulous read and I'm ever so sorry that David Gemmell won't be writing anymore books.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

A fitting and brilliant end to the trilogy and his collection of books. Perfect!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5699197127322655985">This was a bit of a letdown for me after reading the first two books. Granted, it was mostly written by David Gemmell's wife (using a draft he had started and notes for the plot), but it just didn't draw me in like the others. Sadly, the characters and story seemed quite bland in comparison - it felt like more of a telling than an emotional journey. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2290000560" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2290000560" />
    <a title="Sam Stockdale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76688199-sam-stockdale"><img alt="Sam Stockdale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601851061p2/76688199.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2290000560?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Stockdale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Stockdale" href="/user/show/76688199-sam-stockdale">Sam Stockdale</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780552151139" href="/book/show/1850100.Fall_of_Kings">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2290000560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8908217031763863805">What a fantastic conclusion to a fantastic series. This has been one of those stories that I didn't want to end. It's a bit of bummer when you know what the outcome is going to be (I've read The Iliad) but David Gemmell is such a brilliant storyteller (just like Odysseus) that even though you know how it ends, he keeps you guessing and wondering just how he's going to do it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>
